<p>Although arthropods are the most numerous phylum on Earth, and thousands of arthropod species are venomous, they inflict relatively few serious bites and stings on humans. Far more serious are the effects on humans of diseases like <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> carried by blood-sucking insects. Other blood-sucking insects infect livestock with diseases that kill many animals and greatly reduce the usefulness of others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hill1997EconomicImportanceOfInsectsP7To92_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hill1997EconomicImportanceOfInsectsP7To92-142">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tick" title="Tick">Ticks</a> can cause <a href="/wiki/Tick_paralysis" title="Tick paralysis">tick paralysis</a> and several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasite</a>-borne diseases in humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup> A few of the closely related <a href="/wiki/Mite" title="Mite">mites</a> also infest humans, causing intense itching,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup> and others cause <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">allergic</a> diseases, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hay_fever" title="Hay fever">hay fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eczema" title="Eczema">eczema</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many species of arthropods, principally insects but also mites, are agricultural and forest pests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPM_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPM-146">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> The mite <i><a href="/wiki/Varroa_destructor" title="Varroa destructor">Varroa destructor</a></i> has become the largest single problem faced by <a href="/wiki/Beekeeper" title="Beekeeper">beekeepers</a> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[143]</a></sup> Efforts to control arthropod pests by large-scale use of <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> have caused long-term effects on human health and on <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[144]</a></sup> Increasing arthropod <a href="/wiki/Pesticide_resistance" title="Pesticide resistance">resistance</a> to pesticides has led to the development of <a href="/wiki/Integrated_pest_management" title="Integrated pest management">integrated pest management</a> using a wide range of measures including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_control" title="Biological control">biological control</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPM_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-IPM-146">[141]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">Predatory</a> mites may be useful in controlling some mite pests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shultz2001ArachnidsInEncOfLifeSci_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shultz2001ArachnidsInEncOfLifeSci-150">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="As_predators">As predators<span class="anchor" id="Predators"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arthropod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: As predators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Even amongst arthropods usually thought of as obligate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">predators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flower" title="Flower">floral</a> food sources (<a href="/wiki/Nectar" title="Nectar">nectar</a> and to a lesser degree <a href="/wiki/Pollen" title="Pollen">pollen</a>) are often useful adjunct sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-et-al-2021_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-He-et-al-2021-152">[147]</a></sup> It was noticed in one study<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-Sigsgaard-2019_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-He-Sigsgaard-2019-153">[148]</a></sup> that adult <i><a href="/wiki/Adalia_bipunctata" title="Adalia bipunctata">Adalia bipunctata</a></i> (predator and common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_control" title="Biological control">biocontrol</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_flour_moth" title="Mediterranean flour moth">Ephestia kuehniella</a></i>) could survive on flowers but never completed the <a href="/wiki/Biological_life_cycle" title="Biological life cycle">life cycle</a>, so a meta-analysis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-et-al-2021_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-He-et-al-2021-152">[147]</a></sup> was done to find such an overall trend in previously published data, if it existed. In some cases floral resources are outright necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-et-al-2021_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-He-et-al-2021-152">[147]</a></sup> Overall, floral resources (and an imitation, i.e. sugar water) increase <a href="/wiki/Longevity" title="Longevity">longevity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fecundity" title="Fecundity">fecundity</a>, meaning even predatory population numbers can depend on non-prey food abundance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-et-al-2021_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-He-et-al-2021-152">[147]</a></sup> Thus biocontrol success may surprisingly depend on nearby flowers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-He-et-al-2021_152-4"><a href="#cite_note-He-et-al-2021-152">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arthropod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1093669538">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:solid #aaa 1px}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalborder>ul{padding:0.1em;background:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint plainlist portalbox portalborder tright" role="navigation">
<ul>
<li><span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cercophonius_squama.jpg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="1606" data-file-width="1974" decoding="async" height="26" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cercophonius_squama.jpg/32px-Cercophonius_squama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cercophonius_squama.jpg/48px-Cercophonius_squama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cercophonius_squama.jpg/64px-Cercophonius_squama.jpg 2x" width="32"/></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Arthropods" title="Portal:Arthropods">Arthropods portal</a></span></li></ul></div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Invertebrate_paleontology" title="Invertebrate paleontology">Invertebrate paleontology</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arthropod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_New_Zealand" title="Museum of New Zealand">Museum of New Zealand</a> notes that "in everyday conversation", <i>bug</i> "refers to land arthropods with at least six legs, such as insects, spiders, and centipedes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>  In a chapter on "Bugs That Are Not Insects", entomologist Gilbert Walbauer specifies centipedes, millipedes, arachnids (spiders, <a href="/wiki/Opiliones" title="Opiliones">daddy longlegs</a>, scorpions, <a href="/wiki/Mite" title="Mite">mites</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chigger" title="Chigger">chiggers</a> and ticks) as well as the few terrestrial crustaceans (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sowbug" title="Sowbug">sowbugs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pillbug" title="Pillbug">pillbugs</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walbauer5_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walbauer5-9">[9]</a></sup> but argues that "including legless creatures such as worms, slugs, and snails among the bugs stretches the word too much".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walbauer1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walbauer1-10">[10]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"It would be too bad if the question of head segmentation ever should be finally settled; it has been for so long such fertile ground for theorizing that arthropodists would miss it as a field for mental exercise."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The fossil was originally named <i>Eotarbus</i> but was renamed when it was realized that a <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a> arachnid had already been named <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Eotarbus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Eotarbus (page does not exist)">Eotarbus</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-127"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-127">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For a mention of insect contamination in an international food quality standard, see sections 3.1.2 and 3.1.3 of Codex 152 of 1985 of the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Alimentarius" title="Codex Alimentarius">Codex Alimentarius</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For examples of quantified acceptable insect contamination levels in food see the last entry (on "Wheat Flour") and the definition of "Extraneous material" in <i>Codex Alimentarius</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup> and the standards published by the FDA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[125]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFSiebold1848">Siebold, C. (1848). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/lehrbuchdervergl01sieb/page/4" rel="nofollow"><i>Lehrbuch der vergleichenden Anatomie der Wirbellosen Thiere</i></a> [<i>Textbook of Comparative Anatomy of Invertebrate Animals</i>] (in German). Berlin, (Germany): Veit &amp; Co. p. 4. <q><i>"Arthropoda.  Thiere mit vollkommen symmetrischer Form und gegliederten Bewegungsorganen.  Centralmasse des Nervensystems besteht aus einem den Schlund umfassenden Ganglienring und einer von diesem ausgehenden Bauch-Ganglienkette."</i> (Arthropoda.  Animals with completely symmetric form and articulated organs of movement.  Central mass of the nervous system consists of a ring of ganglia surrounding the esophagus and an abdominal chain of ganglia extending from this [ring of ganglia].)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Lehrbuch+der+vergleichenden+Anatomie+der+Wirbellosen+Thiere&amp;rft.place=Berlin%2C+%28Germany%29&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.pub=Veit+%26+Co.&amp;rft.date=1848&amp;rft.aulast=Siebold&amp;rft.aufirst=C.+Th.+v.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Flehrbuchdervergl01sieb%2Fpage%2F4&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArthropod"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFHegnaLeggMøllerVan_Roy2013">Hegna, Thomas A.; Legg, David A.; Møller, Ole Sten; Van Roy, Peter; Lerosey-Aubril, Rudy (November 19, 2013). <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arthropod&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
